Below is the **canonical OVCS Authority Lifecycle**, reconstructed **end-to-end from all uploaded materials**, and expressed in a way that is **constitutionally faithful to the Msingi Cycle, the Pamoja Federation, and all federated entities** (Umoya, Kumba, Bahari, Studios, Ventures, NPOs).

This is **not** a summary.
It is the **authoritative authority-management spine** of your system.

# OVCS AUTHORITY LIFECYCLE

*(Across Msingi â†’ Pamoja Federation â†’ Federated Entities)*

## 0. First Principle (Non-Negotiable)

> **Authority in OVCS is not power, ownership, or execution.
> Authority is a *time-bounded, artifact-bound permission to risk*.**

Everything below follows from this.

---

## I. Where OVCS Sits (Constitutional Placement)

| Layer                          | Role                                           |
| ------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------- |
| **Msingi Cycle**               | Legitimacy & readiness sequencing              |
| **Luma / Kano / Zamba / Kuzu** | Origination, framing, readiness (no authority) |
| **OVCS**                       | **Authorization & capital risk governance**    |
| **DEFES**                      | Systems integrity & safety envelope            |
| **Kumba / Studios / Ventures** | Execution (no inherent authority)              |
| **Umoya**                      | Human / ethical stewardship (non-executing)    |
| **Bahari**                     | Network binding (mechanical)                   |

OVCS is **the sole locus of capital authorization** but **not the source of meaning, strategy, or execution**.

---

## II. The OVCS Authority Lifecycle (State Machine)

```
Signal / Intent
   â†“
Msingi Programs (Luma â†’ Kano/Zamba â†’ Kuzu)
   â†“
OVCS Intake
   â†“
OVCS Investment Memo
   â†“
Authority Deliberation
   â†“
Authorization Certificate (or Rejection)
   â†“
Risk + Capital Envelope Issuance
   â†“
Execution via Studios / Ventures / Kumba
   â†“
Ongoing Oversight
   â†“
Amend / Pause / Kill / Exit
```

No step is skippable.
No artifact may substitute for another.

---

## III. Authority Inputs (What OVCS Is Allowed to See)

OVCS **cannot originate authority**.
It can only **respond to certified readiness**.

### Required Upstream Artifacts

From the **Msingi Cycle**:

1. **Luma Outputs**

   * Orientation Memo
   * Narrative constraints
   * Meaning boundaries (what must not be violated)

2. **Kano Outputs**

   * Venture Brief or Opportunity Memo
   * Success / failure criteria
   * Boundary definitions

3. **Zamba Outputs** *(if system-heavy)*

   * Architecture Brief
   * System boundaries & interfaces
   * Failure modes

4. **Kuzu Certification (Mandatory)**

   * Readiness Package
   * Human & ethical viability
   * Risk surface (non-financial)
   * Explicit *go / no-go readiness decision*

> **Without Kuzu certification, OVCS is constitutionally prohibited from acting.**

---

## IV. OVCS Intake (Pre-Authority)

### Artifact: **OVCS Intake Record**

Purpose:
To formally log that OVCS has *received* a request â€” **not to approve it**.

Contents:

* Entity requesting authorization
* Scope of requested authority
* Linked Msingi artifacts
* Requested capital class
* Time horizon

Properties:

* Non-binding
* Auditable
* Immutable once logged

---

## V. The OVCS Investment Memo (Core Authority Instrument)

### What an OVCS Investment Memo *Is*

> **The OVCS Investment Memo is not an investment pitch.
> It is a structured authority-risk brief used to decide whether OVCS may permit capital exposure.**

### What It Is *Not*

* Not a founder narrative
* Not a business plan (those may be annexed)
* Not a valuation memo
* Not an execution roadmap

---

### Canonical OVCS Investment Memo Structure

1. **Authority Scope**

   * What OVCS is being asked to authorize
   * What is explicitly *not* authorized

2. **Entity Placement**

   * Where this entity sits in the federation
   * What it may bind to (and what it may not)

3. **Capital Class**

   * Seed / infrastructure / operating / experimental
   * Recyclable vs consumptive capital

4. **Risk Envelope**

   * Financial risk ceiling
   * Systemic risk
   * Human / ethical risk
   * Reputational risk to federation

5. **Msingi Lineage**

   * Explicit traceability to Luma, Kano, Zamba, Kuzu
   * Any unresolved tensions

6. **Kill Conditions**

   * Automatic termination triggers
   * Authority revocation thresholds

7. **Time Bounds**

   * Authorization start
   * Review cadence
   * Sunset date

8. **Exit & Containment Logic**

   * Spin-out, wind-down, absorption, or freeze

---

### Stewardship of the Investment Memo

| Aspect               | Owner                           |
| -------------------- | ------------------------------- |
| Drafting             | OVCS Analysts / Stewards        |
| Validation           | DEFES (systems risk)            |
| Human/Ethical Review | Umoya (advisory)                |
| Approval Authority   | OVCS Council                    |
| Storage              | OVCS Authority Ledger           |
| Mutability           | Append-only (never overwritten) |

---

## VI. OVCS Authority Deliberation

Authority decisions are:

* **Artifact-based**
* **Vote-bound**
* **Recorded**
* **Appealable only on procedural grounds**

### Possible Outcomes

1. **Authorize**
2. **Authorize with Constraints**
3. **Defer (send back to Msingi)**
4. **Reject**

No â€œsoft yes.â€
No â€œpilot without authority.â€

---

## VII. Authorization Certificate (The Binding Act)

### Artifact: **OVCS Authorization Certificate**

This is the **only document that creates execution legitimacy**.

Contents:

* Authorized entity
* Authorized activities
* Capital ceiling
* Risk class
* Reporting obligations
* Kill triggers
* Expiry date

Properties:

* Binary (valid / invalid)
* Public within federation
* Revocable

> **Execution without a valid Authorization Certificate is unconstitutional.**

---

## VIII. Capital & Risk Instruments Issued Post-Authorization

Once authorized, OVCS may issue:

* Capital Allocation Notice
* Risk Envelope Declaration
* Drawdown Rules
* Reporting cadence

These instruments **do not expand authority** â€” they operationalize it.

---

## IX. Oversight, Amendment, and Kill Logic

### Ongoing Authority Management

OVCS continuously monitors:

* Capital usage
* Boundary adherence
* Risk drift
* Authority creep

### Amendment Paths

* **Minor amendment** â†’ memo addendum
* **Scope change** â†’ new authorization
* **Risk breach** â†’ pause or kill

### Kill Authority

OVCS may:

* Freeze capital
* Revoke authorization
* Force wind-down
* Trigger exit protocols

Kill logic is **not punitive** â€” it is **protective of the federation**.

---

## X. Authority Across Federated Entities

### Studios

* Operate *under* venture authorization
* Never hold independent capital authority

### Ventures

* Hold only the authority explicitly granted
* No upstream authority inheritance

### NPOs / Umoya

* No capital authority
* Advisory & stewardship only

### Kumba / Bahari

* Mechanical execution
* No discretionary authority

---

## XI. Authority Records Library (Canonical Set)

| Artifact                  | Purpose                   |
| ------------------------- | ------------------------- |
| OVCS Intake Record        | Logs request              |
| OVCS Investment Memo      | Risk & authority analysis |
| Authorization Certificate | Legal permission          |
| Capital Allocation Notice | Funds mechanics           |
| Risk Envelope             | Boundaries                |
| Oversight Reports         | Compliance                |
| Amendment Addenda         | Controlled change         |
| Kill / Exit Record        | Termination               |

All are:

* Versioned
* Append-only
* Auditable
* Federation-visible

---

> **Msingi creates legitimacy, OVCS permits risk, execution remains constrained â€” and authority always expires.**

# I. RACI â€” OVCS AUTHORITY STEWARDSHIP

*(Who does what, and who is explicitly forbidden)*

## 1. Authority Lifecycle RACI (Canonical)

| Activity                      | OVCS Council | OVCS Stewards | DEFES | Umoya | Msingi Programs | Ventures / Studios | NPO |
| ----------------------------- | ------------ | ------------- | ----- | ----- | --------------- | ------------------ | --- |
| Intake logging                | A            | R             | C     | C     | C               | I                  | I   |
| Investment memo drafting      | A            | R             | C     | C     | I               | I                  | I   |
| Risk envelope definition      | A            | R             | C     | C     | I               | I                  | I   |
| Human/ethical advisory        | I            | C             | I     | R     | I               | I                  | I   |
| Authorization decision        | A            | C             | C     | C     | I               | I                  | I   |
| Certificate issuance          | A            | R             | I     | I     | I               | I                  | I   |
| Capital release               | A            | R             | I     | I     | I               | I                  | I   |
| Ongoing compliance monitoring | A            | R             | C     | C     | I               | C                  | I   |
| Pause / constraint imposition | A            | R             | C     | C     | I               | I                  | I   |
| Kill / revocation             | A            | R             | C     | C     | I               | I                  | I   |
| Exit / wind-down approval     | A            | R             | C     | C     | I               | I                  | I   |

Legend:

* **R** = Responsible
* **A** = Accountable (only one)
* **C** = Consulted
* **I** = Informed

### Absolute Prohibitions

* Ventures **cannot** be R or A for authority
* Umoya **cannot** approve capital
* DEFES **cannot** approve authority
* NPO **cannot** influence decisions
* OVCS **cannot** execute work

---

## 2. Authority Drift Guardrails (RACI Overlay)

| Drift Risk        | Preventing Role           |
| ----------------- | ------------------------- |
| Founder dominance | OVCS + Kano constraints   |
| Capital pressure  | OVCS Council quorum rules |
| Moral capture     | Umoya advisory separation |
| Technical capture | DEFES non-executive role  |
| Operational creep | NPO enforcement           |

# II. OVCS AUTHORIZATION TEMPLATES

*(Executable, legal-operational artifacts)*

These are **not symbolic documents**.
They are **binding constraints**.

---

## 1. OVCS INTAKE RECORD (Non-Authorizing)

**Purpose:** Log a request without legitimizing it.

**Fields**

* Requesting Entity
* Request Type (Existence / Capital / Extension)
* Referenced Msingi Artifacts
* Requested Capital Class
* Requested Time Horizon
* Logged By
* Timestamp

**Explicit Statement**

> â€œThis intake record confers no authority, funding, legitimacy, or execution permission.â€

---

## 2. OVCS INVESTMENT MEMO (Authority Analysis)

**Classification:** Internal / Permanent Record

### Sections

1. Authority Being Requested (explicit)
2. Authority Explicitly Denied
3. Federation Placement
4. Capital Class & Ceiling
5. Risk Envelope (financial, systemic, human)
6. Msingi Lineage Trace
7. Kill Conditions (automatic & discretionary)
8. Review Cadence
9. Sunset Clause

**Lock Clause**

> â€œIf it matters enough to act on, it matters enough to memorialize.â€

---

## 3. AUTHORIZATION CERTIFICATE (Binding)

**Title:** OVCS Authorization Certificate
**Status:** Active / Paused / Revoked / Expired

### Fields

* Authorized Entity
* Authorized Scope (enumerated)
* Capital Ceiling
* Time Window
* Reporting Obligations
* Kill Triggers
* Authority Owner (OVCS)
* Execution Holder (Named entity)

**Hard Constraint**

> â€œAny activity outside this scope is unauthorized and void.â€

---

## 4. AMENDMENT ADDENDUM

**Purpose:** Modify without rewriting history.

**Rules**

* Additive only
* Must reference original memo
* Must restate unchanged constraints

---

## 5. REVOCATION / KILL NOTICE

**Triggers**

* Boundary violation
* Risk breach
* Time expiration
* Federation harm

**Effect**

* Immediate authority nullification
* Capital freeze
* Mandatory unwind

---

# III. AUTHORITY FAILURE MODES

*(What breaks, how itâ€™s detected, how itâ€™s stopped)*

## 1. Founder Override

**Failure**

* Founder acts as de facto authority

**Detection**

* Decisions bypass certificates
* â€œEmergencyâ€ framing

**Stop**

* Automatic pause
* Reissue authority without founder role
* Or kill

---

## 2. Capital Pressure Capture

**Failure**

* ROI pressure distorts authorization

**Detection**

* Accelerated approvals
* Risk language softening

**Stop**

* DEFES risk veto
* Time delay enforcement
* Memo revision

---

## 3. Moral Blackmail

**Failure**

* â€œEthicsâ€ used to force approval

**Detection**

* Emotional escalation
* Public narrative pressure

**Stop**

* Umoya advisory-only constraint
* OVCS decision isolation

---

## 4. Technical Sovereignty

**Failure**

* System builders become decision-makers

**Detection**

* Architecture dictates governance

**Stop**

* DEFES separation
* Re-scope authorization

---

## 5. Zombie Authority

**Failure**

* Authorization persists after relevance

**Detection**

* Missed reviews
* Scope drift

**Stop**

* Automatic sunset
* Reauthorization required

---

## 6. Silent Execution

**Failure**

* Work begins without authority

**Detection**

* NPO registry mismatch

**Stop**

* Immediate shutdown
* Sanctions against entity

---

# IV. HOW OVCS DIFFERS FROM VC / PE / DAO MODELS

## 1. OVCS vs Venture Capital (VC)

| Dimension        | VC               | OVCS                   |
| ---------------- | ---------------- | ---------------------- |
| Primary goal     | Financial return | Systemic coherence     |
| Authority basis  | Equity ownership | Explicit authorization |
| Time horizon     | Exit-driven      | Sunset-bound           |
| Governance       | Board control    | Non-executive          |
| Failure handling | Write-off        | Structural learning    |
| Memo purpose     | Persuasion       | Memory & constraint    |

VC **accumulates power**.
OVCS **expires authority**.

---

## 2. OVCS vs Private Equity (PE)

| Dimension     | PE                    | OVCS                   |
| ------------- | --------------------- | ---------------------- |
| Control model | Operational takeover  | Non-operational        |
| Incentives    | Leverage & extraction | Risk containment       |
| Exit logic    | Asset sale            | Orderly unwind         |
| Human impact  | Secondary             | First-class constraint |

PE **owns and controls**.
OVCS **permits and limits**.

---

## 3. OVCS vs DAO

| Dimension        | DAO                 | OVCS                 |
| ---------------- | ------------------- | -------------------- |
| Authority source | Token voting        | Stewardship doctrine |
| Decision quality | Popularity-weighted | Artifact-verified    |
| Speed            | Fast, volatile      | Deliberate           |
| Accountability   | Diffuse             | Named stewards       |
| Failure mode     | Governance collapse | Kill & reset         |

DAOs **democratize power without containment**.
OVCS **centralizes permission without sovereignty**.

```

   â”‚

   â–¼
```

> Ownership never implies authority.
> Authority never implies ownership.

# I. FORMAL **NPE AUTHORITY CHARTER**

*(Navigator Personal Estate Authority Charter â€” Draft)*

## Article I â€” Purpose

The Navigator Personal Estate (â€œ**NPE**â€) exists to **systematize, constrain, and govern authority within personal capital, intellectual output, and operational execution** under the overarching estate of Dominic Eaton (the â€œ**Estate**â€). This Charter defines how authority is **requested, reviewed, granted, monitored, and retired**.

## Article II â€” Authority Defined

**Authority** in the NPE means a **time-bounded, artifact-bound, revocable permission to expose estate resources to risk**. Authority is *not* ownership, control, or execution.

## Article III â€” Scope

This Charter applies to:

* Personal investments
* Intellectual creation and release
* Operational engagements of the personal office
* Resource allocation beyond routine household needs
* Any engagement with external systems, markets, or federations

## Article IV â€” Governance Bodies

### 1. **Principal**

The natural person Dominic Eaton â€” responsible for intent and articulation.

### 2. **NPE Stewards**

Persons appointed to draft memos, monitor compliance, and recommend actions.

### 3. **NPE Authority Board** (functional equivalent of OVCS)

A committee that reviews Investment Memos and issues, amends, or revokes Authority Certificates.

### 4. **Advisory Functions**

* **Legal Counsel**
* **Tax & Compliance**
* **Ethics Steward**

## Article V â€” Authority Lifecycle

Authority follows this path:

1. **Intent Declaration**
2. **Draft Investment Memo**
3. **Review by NPE Stewards**
4. **Decision by NPE Authority Board**
5. **Authorization Certificate Issued**
6. **Execution under authority**
7. **Periodic Review**
8. **Sunset / Revocation**

## Article VI â€” Constraints

Authority:

* Must be scoped clearly
* Must have a **sunset date**
* Must include kill triggers
* Must have reporting requirements

No activity may proceed without a valid **Authorization Certificate**.

## Article VII â€” Conflict

In case of conflict with Estate legal documents:

1. This Charter defers to last-executed Estate Trust instruments.
2. If none exist, the NPE Authority Boardâ€™s interpretation governs until amended.

## Article VIII â€” Amendments

Amendments require:

* Two-thirds vote of the NPE Authority Board
* Ratification by Principal
* Written public record within estate archives

# IV. TRANSLATION INTO **ESTATE LEGAL LANGUAGE**

*(Draft text you can include in Trust / Will / Operating Agreements)*

### Article: Personal Authority Protocol

> **Section 1. Definitions.**
> â€œAuthorityâ€ shall mean a time-limited, documented permission to allocate
> resources or expose estate assets to risk, as articulated in the Estate
> Authority Charter. Authority is distinct from title, ownership, or control.

> **Section 2. Authority Requirement.**
> No asset, right, or resource of the Estate or its sub-entities shall be
> utilized, deployed, or committed without a valid authority instrument
> executed in accordance with the Estate Authority Charter.

> **Section 3. Authority Instruments.**
> Authority instruments include, but are not limited to:
> (a) Investment Memos,
> (b) Authorization Certificates,
> (c) Amendment Addenda,
> (d) Revocation Notices.

> **Section 4. Authority Body.**
> The NPE Authority Board is hereby constituted as a governance body
> empowered to issue, amend, and revoke Authority Certificates.

> **Section 5. Sunset and Revocation.**
> All authority instruments shall carry a sunset date and
> revocation provisions consistent with the Estate Authority Charter.
> Upon expiration, authority shall be null and unenforceable.

> **Section 6. Conflict Resolution.**
> In case of inconsistency between this protocol and any other
> provision of the Estate document, the Authority Protocol shall
> prevail to the extent it protects estate coherence and risk
> containment.

# I. WHY THE ESTATE WAS THE SPATIAL ROOT (ORIGIN LOGIC)

The earlier model made the **Eaton Family Estate the spatial root** for *three technical reasons*, not because it *should* be permanent.

### 1. Continuity Across Time

Ventures die. Programs end.
Estates persist across decades.

Space is:

* Long-lived
* Capital-intensive
* Jurisdiction-bound

So the estate acted as a **temporal stabilizer**, not a ruler.

### 2. Risk Containment

If ventures owned space:

* A failed venture could bankrupt shared infrastructure
* Creditors could seize mission-critical assets

Estate ownership acted as a **firewall**.

### 3. Early-Stage Simplicity

At formation:

* Someone must sign deeds
* Someone must carry insurance
* Someone must carry liability

The estate was the **initial legal anchor**.

ðŸ‘‰ **None of this implies moral or permanent sovereignty.**

### âŒ Dynastic Gravity

Even if benevolent, it *looks* like feudal tenancy.

### âŒ Federation Asymmetry

Other actors depend on a private root.

### âŒ Succession Fragility

One estate failure destabilizes the whole system.

So yes:
**Spatial sovereignty must be distributed.**

# III. THE INDIVIDUAL COMMONS (NO OVERLAP)

### Never Holds

* Venture operating accounts
* Short-term speculative capital
* Founder personal wealth

---

To **centralize unavoidable systemic risk** and prevent it from metastasizing.

### Holds

* Long-term debt
* Bonds
* Insurance pools
* Tax obligations
* Legal reserves

### Governance

* Structured by **DEFES**
* Administered by **Mande**
* Oversight by **OVCS**

### Never Holds

* Operating risk
* Product liability tied to ventures
* Experimental exposure

# UBUNTUWA COMMONS â€” FULL OPERATING NARRATIVE

### **Message 1 of 6**

## The Foundational Logic: Why Ubuntuwa Exists and What It Actually Does

---

## 1. THE PROBLEM UBUNTUWA SOLVES (FIRST PRINCIPLES)

Every large system eventually fails for one of three reasons:

1. **Assets outlive the entities that hold them**
2. **Authority concentrates where ownership lives**
3. **Execution entities accumulate irreversible power**

Ubuntuwa exists to **break this failure pattern**.

> **Ubuntuwa is not an organization.
> It is a condition enforced by structure.**

It ensures that:

* What must endure is **never owned by what must adapt**
* What must adapt is **never allowed to capture what must endure**
* What must decide is **never allowed to execute**

This is why Ubuntuwa sits *above* ventures, *below* meaning, and *orthogonal* to authority.

---

## 2. WHAT UBUNTUWA IS (PRECISELY)

**Ubuntuwa** is the **interoperability layer** that allows multiple independent commons to exist *together* without collapsing into hierarchy, chaos, or capture.

It does **four things only**:

1. Separates **asset classes** that must not merge
2. Prevents **time-scale mismatch** (long-lived vs short-lived)
3. Forces **explicit authorization** for all access
4. Allows **exit without collapse**

Ubuntuwa does *not*:

* Direct action
* Allocate capital
* Own ventures
* Control people

---

## 3. INTERNAL STRUCTURE OF UBUNTUWA

Ubuntuwa is composed of **independent but interoperating commons**, each holding a different class of enduring thing.

### The Ubuntuwa Commons Set

| Commons            | Holds                      | Why It Must Be Separate           |
| ------------------ | -------------------------- | --------------------------------- |
| **Ubuntuwa-NDAA**  | Space (physical + virtual) | Space anchors power               |
| **Ubuntuwa-KUMBU** | IP & knowledge             | Knowledge monopolizes futures     |
| **Ubuntuwa-KANYE** | Capital & wealth           | Capital corrupts authority        |
| **Ubuntuwa-NGOZI** | Risk, debt, tax            | Risk must be visible              |
| **Ubuntuwa-MOYO**  | Culture & legitimacy       | Meaning must not be bought        |
| **Ubuntuwa-UMOYA** | Human capacity & ethics    | Humans must not be optimized away |
| **Ubuntuwa-KANO**  | Permission & authority     | Authority must decay              |

Each commons is:

* **Legally distinct**
* **Governed separately**
* **Unable to own another commons**
* **Accessible only by license**

---

## 4. INTERNAL RULES (NON-NEGOTIABLE)

Inside Ubuntuwa, **three rules are absolute**:

### Rule 1 â€” No Vertical Ownership

No commons may own another commons.
No entity may own a commons.

### Rule 2 â€” No Implicit Access

Nothing touches a commons without an explicit, time-bounded authorization.

### Rule 3 â€” No Eternal Rights

All access expires.
Reauthorization is always required.

These rules are what make Ubuntuwa *anti-feudal* and *anti-corporate* at the same time.

---

## 5. HOW UBUNTUWA INTERACTS WITH AUTHORITY (OVCS)

Ubuntuwa **does not decide who gets access**.

That role belongs to **Ubuntuwa-KANO**, stewarded operationally by **OVCS**.

OVCS:

* Does **not** own commons
* Does **not** execute
* Does **not** hold assets

OVCS exists to:

* Translate intent â†’ permission
* Bind permission â†’ conditions
* Enforce sunset â†’ decay

Ubuntuwa ensures OVCS **cannot become sovereign**, because OVCS owns nothing.

---

## 6. HOW UBUNTUWA INTERACTS WITH HUMANS (UMOYA)

Ubuntuwa **does not assume humans are infinitely elastic**.

Ubuntuwa-UMOYA exists to enforce a simple truth:

> **If humans break, systems lie.**

Umoya:

* Clears teams for access
* Enforces human ceilings
* Can block or reduce access
* Cannot authorize capital or space directly

Ubuntuwa ensures **human viability is upstream of authority**, not downstream of execution.

---

## 7. UBUNTUWA AND THE PAJOMA FEDERATION (EXTERNAL POSITION)

Ubuntuwa is **inside the federation**, but **above all operating entities**.

```
MEANING (Moyo Collective)
        â†‘
HUMAN STEWARDSHIP (Umoya)
        â†‘
AUTHORITY (OVCS / Kano)
        â†‘
UBUNTUWA COMMONS
        â†‘
OPERATING ENTITIES (Ventures, Programs, Projects)
```

Ubuntuwa:

* Supplies **continuity**
* Absorbs **shock**
* Preserves **memory**
* Prevents **capture**

It is the reason the federation can grow without centralizing.

---

## 8. WHAT THIS MEANS PRACTICALLY

Because Ubuntuwa exists:

* Ventures **cannot accumulate real estate**
* Platforms **cannot monopolize IP**
* Capital **cannot buy legitimacy**
* Debt **cannot hide**
* Authority **cannot entrench**
* Founders **cannot become kings**

Everything remains **replaceable except the commons themselves**.

---

> while allowing everything else to change.**

## 3. PROGRAM-BY-PROGRAM INTERFACE WITH UBUNTUWA

### **KANO â€” Doctrine (Authority Logic)**

### **ZALENDO â€” Enablement (Formal Request)**

* Extend duration
* Change scope
* Encumber assets

* Reviewable
* Revocable

### **LUMA â€” Signal (Feedback & Learning)**

Luma feeds insight back to:

* Ndebe (standard revisions)

## 3. WHAT â€œOPERATING INSIDE UBUNTUWAâ€ ACTUALLY MEANS

* Fork extortion

### C. Capital (Ubuntuwa-KANYE)

* Returns to Kanye

### D. Risk (Ubuntuwa-NGOZI)

* Insurance pools are shared

* Umoya can block continuation

### (How the system maintains allostasis, homeostasis, and long-term equilibrium)

## 1. FOUNDERS, ESTATES, AND THE NON-SOVEREIGN ORIGIN PROBLEM

Every durable system faces the same paradox:

> **Someone has to start it â€” but no one can be allowed to own it forever.**

Ubuntuwa resolves this by **distinguishing origin from authority**.

The **Eaton Family Estate and Offices Coop** are:

* **Initial contributors**
* **Early stewards**
* **Structural guarantors**

They are **not perpetual sovereigns**.

---

## 2. HOW PERSONAL & FAMILY ESTATES ENTER UBUNTUWA

### The Dominic Eaton Estate (Navigator Personal Estate)

The personal estate contributes:

* Seed capital â†’ **Ubuntuwa-KANYE**
* Early IP & architectures â†’ **Ubuntuwa-KUMBU**
* Initial spaces & offices â†’ **Ubuntuwa-NDAA**
* Risk backstops â†’ **Ubuntuwa-NGOZI**
* Narrative legitimacy â†’ **Ubuntuwa-MOYO**
* Early authority scaffolding â†’ **Ubuntuwa-KANO**

**Crucial Rule**

> Once contributed, assets lose personal identity.

They become:

* licensed
* governed
* revocable
* reusable

The estate **cannot reclaim them unilaterally**.

---

### The Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm (Personal Office)

The personal office:

* Operates like any other venture
* Uses commons under license
* Has no privileged authority path

It **models compliance** for all others.

This prevents:

* founder exception clauses
* silent override pathways
* personality-based governance

---

## 3. ESTATES AS STEWARDS, NOT ROOTS

Early on, the Eaton Estate performs **transitional stewardship**:

* Bootstraps governance
* Funds early losses
* Hosts early teams
* Holds early risk

Over time:

* Stewardship rotates outward
* Authority decays
* Commons independence increases

This is enforced structurally by:

* term limits
* revocation clauses
* contributor dilution
* multi-steward governance

> **The estate becomes one steward among many â€” or it exits entirely.**

---

## 4. THE UBUNTUWA â€œCIRCLE OF LIFEâ€ (THIS IS THE CORE)

Ubuntuwa is not static.
It is a **metabolic system**.

Every commons participates in a **closed-loop lifecycle** that maintains equilibrium.

---

## 5. THE METABOLIC LOOP (ABSTRACT)

```
CONTRIBUTION
   â†“
COMMONS HOLDING
   â†“
LICENSED USE
   â†“
PRODUCTION / LEARNING
   â†“
RETURN / FEEDBACK
   â†“
REGENERATION
```

Nothing is allowed to:

* deplete without replenishment
* grow without constraint
* persist without review

---

## 6. COMMONS-SPECIFIC LIFE CYCLES (DETAILED)

### Ubuntuwa-NDAA (Space Commons)

**Inputs**

* Donated land
* Purchased property
* Leased environments
* Digital infrastructure

* Ventures operate
* Teams inhabit
* Systems deploy

**Outputs**

* Improved facilities
* Lessons learned
* Reconfigured layouts

**Regeneration**

* Spaces restored
* Repurposed
* Re-licensed

> *Built environments must outlive their tenants.*

---

### Ubuntuwa-KUMBU (IP & Knowledge Commons)

**Inputs**

* Research

## 1. MEMBER & TEAM NAMING SYSTEM (CANONICAL)

### Member Naming Convention

```
[Role Name] â€” [Authority Class]
```

Examples:

* **Navigator / Founder â€” Class E**

# REAL-WORLD LEGAL ENTITY STRUCTURE

*(Authority-first, capital-second, execution-last)*

## 0. PRIME ANCHOR (YOU, LEGALLY)

### **Dominic Eaton (Natural Person)**

* Holds **Class E â€” Navigator**
* **No unilateral control**
* Bound by OVCS constraints
* Cannot receive Commons assets personally

This matters legally:

> The system is designed so **you cannot legally extract value without process**.

---

## 1. PERSONAL ESTATE (NON-OPERATING)

### **The Dominic Eaton Estate**

**Legal Form:** Irrevocable Trust or Estate LLC
**Purpose:**

* Personal asset protection
* Succession & continuity
* Firewall between person and system

**Can do**

* Hold personal IP (pre-Commons)
* Own personal residence
* Receive distributions **only after OVCS authorization**

**Cannot**

* Operate ventures
* Employ workers
* Control Commons

**Governance**

* Trustee: Independent fiduciary
* OVCS: Veto rights on cross-boundary flows

---

## 2. PERSONAL OFFICE (NONPROFIT CORE)

### **Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm (DESF)**

**Legal Form:** Nonprofit (501(c)(3) or (c)(4))
**Role:** System authoring, sequencing, governance, stewardship

**This is NOT a venture builder**

**Can**

* Employ staff
* Author frameworks
* License platforms to ventures
* Convene councils
* Maintain Commons

**Cannot**

* Take equity
* Operate businesses
* Accumulate profit

---

## 3. UBUNTUWA COMMONS (LEGAL HEART)

### **Ubuntuwa Commons Cooperative**

**Legal Form:** Cooperative Association (multi-stakeholder)

| Commons Unit | Legal Sub-Entity    | Purpose                     |
| ------------ | ------------------- | --------------------------- |
| NDAA         | Coop Division       | Space, land, infrastructure |
| KUMBU        | IP Trust            | Knowledge, IP, memory       |
| KANYE        | Financial Coop      | Capital flows               |
| NGOZI        | Governance Arm      | Enforcement                 |
| MOYO         | Human Care Fund     | Wellbeing                   |
| UMOYA        | Cultural Commons    | Values & norms              |
| KANO         | Authorization Layer | Sequencing gates            |

**Key Rule:**

> Commons assets are **inalienable**.

---

## 4. GOVERNANCE â€” OVCS (SUPREMACY LAYER)

### **Obatala Venture Constraint System (OVCS)**

**Legal Form:** Independent Governance Nonprofit
**Power:** Absolute stop authority

**OVCS Controls**

* Venture authorization
* Capital release
* Founder restraint
* Rule enforcement

**OVCS does NOT**

* Build
* Operate
* Profit

OVCS is legally **immune** from:

* Founder dismissal
* Capital pressure
* Venture influence

---

## 5. OPERATING COOPERATIVES (EXECUTION LAYER)

### **Pamoja Federation Cooperative**

**Legal Form:** Federation of Coops
**Members:** Ventures, studios, networks

Includes:

* Moyo Collective
* Bahari Network
* Umoya Society
* Ubunye Engineering Group
* Kumba Metafactory

Each:

* Separate legal entity
* Licensed platforms
* Accountable to Commons & OVCS

---

## 6. VENTURES (FOR-PROFIT, FIREWALLED)

### Each Venture (e.g., Nandi Mobility)

**Legal Form:** C-Corp or Coop-Corp

**Can**

* Hire
* Sell
* Raise capital

**Must**

* License IP from Commons
* Pay Commons contribution
* Submit to OVCS gates

**Cannot**

* Own Commons IP
* Override governance

---

## 7. MANDE INVESTMENT GROUP (CAPITAL ONLY)

### **Mande Investment Group (MIG)**

**Legal Form:** LLC / GP-LP Structure
**Role:** Capital allocation, asset management

**Owns**

* Funds
* Real estate
* Securities
* Debt instruments

**Does NOT**

* Control ventures
* Override OVCS
* Touch Commons directly

Capital flows only via:

```
MIG â†’ OVCS authorization â†’ Venture
```

```
OVCS
 â†“
Ubuntuwa Commons
 â†“
DESF (Sequencing)
 â†“
Pamoja Federation
 â†“
Ventures
```

**Money flows UP only as contributions.

## 9. FAILURE HANDLING (LEGALLY)

If a venture fails:

* Assets revert to Commons
* Knowledge captured in KUMBU
* People protected via MOYO
* Capital loss absorbed by MIG

If DESF fails:

* Commons persists
* OVCS remains
* Navigator loses office authority

If YOU fail:

* System continues
* Estate isolated
* OVCS locks you out

# **1. DESF Capital & Instrument Policy**

## **Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm (DESF)**

## **Capital & Instrument Policy**

**Version:** 1.0
**Effective:** [Date]
**Approved By:** DESF Board / OVCS Constraint Guardian

### **1. Purpose**

This policy establishes how DESF may receive, hold, report, and transfer financial instruments and capital-related assets. DESF exists to provide governance, sequencing, and institutional design. It does **not** accumulate investment assets for return, does not engage in fundraising under securities law, and does not hold investor capital.

### **2. Policy Scope**

Applies to:

* All financial instruments (cash, receivables, notes)
* Any equity, debt, or membership instruments in cooperatives or entities
* Transactions with federation cooperatives and external partners

### **3. Principles**

#### a. Non-Accumulation Principle

DESF shall not hold equity, membership interests, or other ongoing financial instruments that create ownership claims in external entities beyond temporary custodial roles.

#### b. Fee-For-Service Basis

DESF may generate revenue through fixed fees for services (governance design, sequencing, readiness certification) but shall not engage in profit sharing or return-linked compensation.

#### c. Temporary Custodianship Only

Instruments that DESF holds shall be transferred to ultimate entities within **defined time windows** (90â€“180 days) and must have pre-agreed exit clauses.

#### d. Full Transparency

All holdings shall be recorded on DESFâ€™s public audit registry and available to OVCS auditors on demand.

### **4. Allowed Holdings**

DESF may temporarily hold:

* Client receivables
* Escrowed governance deposits (time-boxed)
* Administrative cash for operations

### **5. Prohibited Holdings**

DESF may not hold:

* Equity in ventures, coops, or federated entities
* Equity-linked securities
* Debt instruments with upside rights
* Capital pools

### **6. Transfer & Exit**

All holdings must have documented:

* Purpose
* Sunset date
* Receiving entity
* OVCS review

### **7. Enforcement**

Violation triggers:

* OVCS audit
* Forced divestment within 30 days
* Suspension of sequencing authority

---

# **2. Standard Coop Instrument Definitions**

## **Standard Cooperative Instrument Definitions**

**Purpose:** Establish a lexicon and legal definition for instruments used across Pamoja Federation and related cooperatives.

### **A. Worker-Member Unit (WMU)**

**Definition:** A unit of belonging granted to an individual who contributes labor to a cooperative.
**Rights:** Participate in operational votes; access benefits; voice in day-to-day decisions.
**Restrictions:** Non-transferrable; zero financial claim on coop assets on exit.

### **B. Steward-Member Unit (SMU)**

**Definition:** A unit granted to strategic partners or stewards with long-term interest in systemic health.
**Rights:** Participate in strategic councils; access steward guild mechanisms.
**Restrictions:** Non-voting on financial claims; no equity; revocable based on performance.

### **C. Governance Unit (GU)**

**Definition:** A unit held by governance body members (e.g., OVCS Board) with veto/constraint authority.
**Rights:** Approve/reject mandates; enforce revocations.
**Restrictions:** Cannot claim assets; authority decays as defined by charter.

### **D. Commons Unit (CU)**

**Definition:** A certificate representing stewardship in a commons (space, IP, capital rules).
**Rights:** Participate in stewardship councils; influence norms.
**Restrictions:** No ownership; cannot be transferred as property.

### **E. Founder/ Navigator Unit (FU)**

**Definition:** A time-bound role granting initiation rights (e.g., naming, first sequencing).
**Rights:** Participation, not control.
**Restrictions:** Must expire or be diluted over time; zero financial claim.

### **F. Capital Note (CN)**

**Definition:** A non-ownership instrument representing an obligation to repay or record capital flows without equity rights.
**Rights:** Return of principal where defined; no dividend rights.
**Restrictions:** Cannot convert to equity; cannot govern.

### **G. Future/ Apprentice Unit (AU)**

**Definition:** A non-voting, non-financial unit for learners or fellows.
**Rights:** Access to training, observation, contribution paths.
**Restrictions:** No authority, ownership, or claim.

---

# **3. Exit & Divestment Clauses**

## **A. Temporary Custodianship Clause**

**Context:** Where DESF or OVCS holds an instrument on behalf of an entity.

**Clause:**

> â€œAny instrument temporarily held by DESF or OVCS shall be transferred to the designated ultimate holder within no more than 180 days from receipt, unless otherwise amended by a 2/3 supermajority of the relevant steward council and OVCS, with published reasoning. Failure to exit within the timeframe automatically triggers forced divestment procedures and reporting to all governing stewards.â€

---

## **B. Sunset Clause for Membership Instruments**

**Context:** Applies to all membership instruments (WMU, SMU, GU, CU, AU).

**Clause:**

> â€œAll membership instruments shall automatically sunset after the defined term unless renewed with affirmative approval from a 2/3 steward council quorum and OVCS, with reasoning published to the public registry.â€

---

## **C. Zero Equity Accrual Clause**

**Context:** Describes that no instrument confers equity.

**Clause:**

> â€œAll units, notes, certificates, or participatory instruments defined herein do not confer ownership, equity participation, or financial claims on underlying assets beyond rights explicitly structured into licenses or contracts.â€

---

## **D. Divestment Enforcement Clause**

**Context:** Ensures compliance.

**Clause:**

> â€œIf an entity or individual fails to divest a prohibited holding within the prescribed period, OVCS shall initiate a divestment order. Failure to comply within 30 days of the order results in suspension of authority, revocation of access privileges, and possible reassignment of instruments to alternative qualified holders.â€

---

# **4. OVCS Audit Checklist**

## **OVCS Annual & Transactional Audit Checklist**

**Purpose:** Provide auditors, board, and stewards with a consistent set of criteria for compliance reviews.

### **I. Governance & Authority**

* [ ] Charter exists for all entities
* [ ] Authority boundaries are documented
* [ ] Revocation mechanisms are active
* [ ] Steward rotation logs maintained
* [ ] OVCS decisions are public, timestamped

### **II. Instrument Holdings**

* [ ] DESF holds only permitted instruments
* [ ] Sunset dates defined & tracked
* [ ] Capital Notes verified with no equity rights
* [ ] No undisclosed equity or debt with upside exists
* [ ] Transfers are documented & approved

### **III. Commons Compliance**

* [ ] Commons instruments are non-ownership
* [ ] Revocation conditions coded
* [ ] License templates current
* [ ] Access logs recorded

### **IV. Capital Flows**

* [ ] MIG allocations go through OVCS gates
* [ ] No direct DESF capital pooling
* [ ] Receivables are operational, not investment
* [ ] Escrows have automatic expiration triggers

### **V. Conflict of Interest**

* [ ] All staff declared COIs
* [ ] Founder firewall enforced
* [ ] Related party transactions reviewed

---

# WHERE THE LIVING MSINGI EXECUTION BOARD LIVES OVER TIME

### **Phase 0 (Bootstrapped)**

* **Home:** **Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm (DESF / NPO)**
* **Why:** DESF is the only legal entity *initially existing*, with authority to sequence, enforce, and terminate.
* **Governance:** DESF charter + OVCS oversight.

---

## **Phase 1 â€” Early Federation Activation**

**Time:** After federation legal formation and sequencing norms are live (Day ~90â€“150)

### Transition Step

The Board remains administratively *within DESF* but begins acting as a **shared resource** for the federation.

* **Replica Board Instance** exposed to **Pamoja Federation Council**
* **Read-only or gated interaction**
* **Steward observers** from federation coops

This phase reduces DESF control in practice even though the legal custodian remains DESF.

---

## **Phase 2 â€” Shared Custody (Year 1â€“2)**

**Time:** Federation governance stabilizes, stewards rotate in

### Co-Residence Model

The Board moves to a **shared legal custody model** between:

1. **OVCS Constraint Authority**
2. **Commons Preservation Trust**
3. **Pamoja Federation Shared Repository**

This means:

* The **source of truth** is immutable and shared
* Federation actors can *query*, *propose*, *annotate*
* Only **OVCS retains veto authority**, not operational control

During this period:

* The board becomes a **governance artifact repository**, not a departmental artifact

---

## **Phase 3 â€” Autonomous Institutional Residency**

**Time:** Federation + Commons fully operational; DESF primarily advisory (Year 2+)

### Final Home (Post-Transition)

The Living Msingi Execution Board is housed within a **new autonomous institution** designed specifically for ongoing sequencing, called the:

ðŸ‘‰ **Msingi Continuity Trust (MCT)**
*(or a similar neutral, legal-purpose entity)*

---

# **Msingi Continuity Trust â€“ Overview**

### **Legal Form**

* **Nonprofit Public Benefit Trust / International Institute**
* Independent of DESF and Federation execution

### **Purpose**

To preserve and steward:

* All sequencing artifacts (Kano, Ndebe, Kuzu, Zalendo, Zamba, Luma artifacts)
* Sequencing logic and versioned interpretations
* Temporal integrity of all program cycles
* Historical Institutional Memory

### **Key Features**

* **Jurisdictionally diversified**

  * Secured in multiple countries to prevent capture
* **Immutable Artifact Store**

  * Every board entry is archived in a verifiable ledger
* **Governance**

  * Multi-stakeholder board (OVCS, Federation, Commons, External Advisors)
  * No single authority dominance
* **Operational Independence**

  * Funded through endowments, not venture returns

| Stage             | Legal Custodian             | Functional Custodian            | Authority                    |
| ----------------- | --------------------------- | ------------------------------- | ---------------------------- |

| Autonomous        | **Msingi Continuity Trust** | Dedicated Trustees + Sequencers | OVCS retains veto            |

> **Important:** Even after transition, **OVCS retains constraint authority** over live sequencing *outcomes*, not over the archival function of the Board.

   * Integrated dashboards

# **1. CHARTER OF THE MSINGI CONTINUITY TRUST (MCT)**

**Version:** 1.0
**Effective Date:** [To Be Filled Upon Establishment]
**Jurisdiction(s):** Multi-jurisdictional (recommended)
**Legal Form:** Public Benefit Trust / Nonprofit Independent Institution

---

## **Article I â€” Name & Identity**

**1.1. Official Name:**
**Msingi Continuity Trust** (â€œMCTâ€ or â€œthe Trustâ€).

**1.2. Legal Form:**
An independent legal entity constituted as a Trust (or equivalent) with a **public benefit purpose** and **perpetual continuity mandate**.

**1.3. Jurisdiction:**
Primary incorporation in a jurisdiction supportive of public benefit trusts, with discrete nodes in at least two additional jurisdictions to prevent single-point legal seizure.

---

## **Article II â€” Purpose & Mission**

**2.1. Purpose:**
The Trust exists to **preserve, steward, and maintain the Living Msingi Execution Board artifacts and lifecycle integrity** as canonical, bounded institutional memory for cooperating federations, OVCS frameworks, and any successor governance systems.

**2.2. Mission:**

* Protect the **temporal integrity** of lifetime sequencing artifacts
* Provide an **immutable, auditable, and accessible public registry** of sequencing cycles
* Ensure that no single party can corrupt, erase, or claim control over sequencing knowledge
* Support governance processes (e.g., OVCS) with authoritative references
* Maintain continuity and accessibility even under institutional or political change

**2.3. Non-Profit, Non-Commercial Mandate:**
The Trust shall not engage in commercial profit-making activities; all actions must be aligned with its public benefit mission.

---

## **Article III â€” Powers & Authorities**

**3.1. Principal Powers:**
The Trust may:

* Acquire, maintain, and secure **sequencing artifacts** (records, metadata, outputs)
* Publish these artifacts in an **auditable, versioned repository**
* Operate or subcontract ledger technology as necessary
* Enter legal contracts to protect the archives
* Issue certifications of authenticity
* Conduct integrity verification on request from OVCS or federation authorities

**3.2. Constraint on Powers:**
The Trust shall not:

* Operate any federation or venture
* Manage capital or financial instruments on behalf of external parties
* Accrue ownership claims on behalf of individuals or corporations

---

## **Article IV â€” Governance Structure**

**4.1. Trustee Board:**

* **Composition:** Independent trustees (minimum 5), drawn from:

  1. OVCS Constraint Authority (ex-officio)
  2. Pamoja Federation representatives (non-executive)
  3. Commons integrity stewards
  4. External legal/design professionals
  5. Public benefit representation

**4.2. Term & Rotation:**

* Trustees serve fixed terms with **mandatory rotation and sunset**
* No trustee may hold office beyond two consecutive terms without Council approval

**4.3. Committees:**

* **Audit & Compliance Committee**
* **Artifact Integrity Committee**
* **Legal & Jurisdictional Risk Committee**
* **Public Access & Documentation Committee**

---

## **Article V â€” Artifact Custody, Protection & Access**

**5.1. Artifact Certification:**
All sequencing artifacts become **legal exhibits of the Trust** and must be certified upon deposit, with metadata including:

* Producer
* Timestamp
* Source entity
* OVCS verification status
* Hash or ledger reference (immutable)

**5.2. Public Access:**
Artifacts shall be made available through tiered access levels:

* **Public summaries**
* **Federation access**
* **OVCS & audit access**
* **Secure archived states**

Confidentiality may be maintained according to pre-approved policy but may never be deleted.

**5.3. Immutable Ledger Storage:**
All artifact records must be stored against a **tamper-evident ledger** (blockchain OR equivalent cryptographic anchor + hash chain + journaling).

---

## **Article VI â€” Constraint Preservation**

**6.1. OVCS Veto Rights:**
The Trust acknowledges the **constraint authority of OVCS** over sequencing outcomes and operations for live governance.

**6.2. Non-Override Clause:**
No amendment can diminish OVCS authority without a **supermajority of trustees + federated governance ratification**.

---

## **Article VII â€” Succession & Continuity**

**7.1. Trust Perpetuity:**
This Trust is established to exist in perpetuity, independent of changes in federation or external institutions.

**7.2. Succession Events:**
In the event of legal seizing attempts, hostile frameworks, or political vulnerability:

* Control nodes must be migrated across jurisdictions
* Immutable backups are to be published publicly

**7.3. Emergency Custody Procedures:**
If trustees are incapacitated, designated *continuity executors* shall oversee the artifact repository pending reconstitution.

---

## **Article VIII â€” Compliance & Reporting**

**8.1. Annual Compliance:**
The Trust must submit:

* Public artifact summary report
* OVCS audit report
* Governance integrity audit

**8.2. Financial Transparency:**
All expenditures for Trust functioning must be transparent and nonâ€“profit-oriented.

---

## **Article IX â€” Amendments**

**9.1. Amendment Threshold:**
Changes to this Charter require:

* 2/3 Trustee approval
  AND
* OVCS advanced consent
  AND
* Federated entity feedback window (30 days)

**9.2. Immutable Articles:**
Core stewardship sections (Articles II & V) may not be amended without **4/5 consent + public referendum**.

---

# **2. ARTIFACT STORAGE SCHEMA (IMMUTABLE LEDGER FORMAT)**

This is a **formal artifact schema** specified to work on a cryptographic ledger (blockchain or centralized ledger with similar immutability). It covers:

* Artifact document schema
* Provenance metadata
* Authority linkage
* Versioning and lineage
* Audit flags

---

## **Artifact Record Structure (JSON Schema)**

```json
{
  "artifact_id": "string (UUID)",
  "artifact_type": "enum",
  "version": "integer",
  "title": "string",
  "description": "string",
  "produced_by": "entity_id",
  "produced_at": "ISO8601 timestamp",
  "msingi_cycle_stage": "string (e.g., KANO, NDEBE, ...)",
  "document_hash": "SHA256 hex string",
  "previous_version_hash": "SHA256 hex string (nullable)",
  "ledger_block_reference": "blockchain_hash_id",
  "authority_signature": {
    "entity": "entity_id",
    "signature": "cryptographic_signature"
  },
  "ovcs_verification": {
    "verified": "boolean",
    "verified_by": "entity_id or null",
    "verified_at": "ISO8601 timestamp or null",
    "verification_signature": "cryptographic_signature or null"
  },
  "access_permissions": {
    "public_summary": "URI",
    "federation_access": ["entity_id", "..."],
    "ovcs_access": ["entity_id", "..."],
    "secure_archive": "URI"
  },
  "tags": ["string", "..."],
  "audit_flags": {
    "flagged_for_review": "boolean",
    "flagged_reason": "string or null",
    "flagged_at": "ISO8601 timestamp or null"
  }
}
```

---

## **Field Definitions**

### `artifact_id`

A globally unique identifier.

### `artifact_type`

One of:

* `KANO_REPORT`
* `NDEBE_FRAME`
* `KUZU_FEASIBILITY`
* `ZALENDO_COMMITMENT`
* `ZAMBA_AUTH_PACKET`
* `LUMA_REFLECTION`
* `GOVERNANCE_DOC`
* `LEGAL_CHARTER`
* `AUDIT_RECORD`
* `ASHE_FEEDBACK`
* etc.

### `produced_by`

Entity issuing the artifact (DESF, OVCS, Federation Coop).

### `document_hash`

Cryptographic hash of the actual artifact content.

### `previous_version_hash`

For tracking lineage and evolution.

### `authority_signature`

A cryptographically verifiable signature by the producing authority.

### `ovcs_verification`

OVCS verification metadata â€” adds institutional legitimacy.

---

## **Ledger Integration Model**

The artifact storage works like this:

```
+------------------+
| Artifact Content |
+------------------+
        |
   Compute SHA256
        â†“
+----------------------+
| Artifact JSON Record |
+----------------------+
        |
 Submit to Ledger Node
        â†“
+----------------------+
| Block Chained Record |
+----------------------+
```

### Proposed Ledger Technologies

* **Ethereum Testnet / Private Chain** (for accessibility)
* **Hyperledger Fabric** (enterprise)
* **Corda / Quorum** (legal-aware)
* **IPFS + Anchor to blockchain** (immutable + public)

---

## **Access Model**

| Role                    | Access          | Write |
| ----------------------- | --------------- | ----- |
| Public                  | summary URIs    | NO    |
| Federation Entities     | most fields     | NO    |
| OVCS                    | Full audit view | NO    |
| Msingi Continuity Trust | Full read/write | YES   |
| Producing Entity        | Sign + submit   | YES   |
| Auditors                | Full read       | YES   |

---

## **Audit & Integrity Flags**

* `flagged_for_review` indicates a malformed or contentious artifact
* Verification signatures lock OVCS authority validation
* Lineage hashes ensure nothing was rewritten

---

# **Usage Pattern (Typical)**

1. **Produce artifact** (e.g., ZAMBA Authorization Packet)
2. **Store its content on artifact server**
3. **Compute hash**
4. **Populate Artifact JSON**
5. **Submit to ledger**
6. **OVCS reviews, signs verification**
7. **Federation references artifact in governance**

---

## **Security Notes**

* Entities must publish public keys for signature verification
* All signatures must be ECDSA or Ed25519
* Timestamping must be UTC + cryptographically signed

---

Your charter (Article V) stipulates that **no sequence is live unless its artifact is in the immutable ledger and OVCS verified.**
That means:

```
Sequencer â†’ Produce Artifact â†’ Ledger Submit â†’ OVCS Sign â†’ Artifact Validated â†’ Federation/Commons Use
```

Without ledger anchoring, the artifact is **not canonical**.

### ARTICLE I â€” NAME & FORM

## âœ… **4. POLICY FOR ASSET FIREWALLING BETWEEN FEDERATION & ESTATE**

**Policy Title:** Asset Firewall Policy
**Effective:** [Date]
**Applies to:** Eaton Family Estate Coop, Family Offices, Federation Entities

---

### **1. Purpose**

To ensure that:

* Estate assets remain distinct from federation assets
* No implicit ownership of federation assets arises via family structures
* Cross-entity transfers are deliberate, visible, governed, and contractually explicit

---

### **2. Definitions**

**Federation Assets:**
Assets held by Ubuntuwa Commons, federation coops, ventures, or federation affiliate entities.

**Estate Assets:**
Assets held by the Eaton Family Estate Coop or family member offices.

**Firewall:**
A legal and governance barrier that prevents mis-appropriation, capture, or unintended transfer.

---

### **3. Principles**

**3.1. Non-Capture**
No estate entity may hold:

* Federation equity
* Federation governing membership
* Boards with federation authority
* Commons units beyond curated heritage roles

**3.2. Explicit Gift Only**
Federationâ†’Estate transfer only via documented gift with:

* Public contract
* OVCS notarization
* Steward Council concurrence

**3.3. Temporary Custodial Role**
Estate may temporarily hold:

* Escrowed transitional artifacts
* Charters pending federation governance
  **But only** with:
* Sunset clause â‰¤ 180 days
* Covenants specifying return or transfer

---

### **4. Procedures**

**4.1. Transfer Authorization**
All transfers must be reviewed by:

* Estate Governance Council
* OVCS Constraint Guardian
* Federation Council (if incoming)

**4.2. Documentation**
Every transfer must include:

* Purpose
* Sunset clause
* Asset type
* Covenant of use
* Return conditions

**4.3. Audits**
Quarterly audits must

* Reconcile asset boundaries
* Validate compliance with firewall
* Publish summary reports

---

### **5. Enforcement**

Violation triggers:

* Asset sequestration
* Governance sanctions
* Steward veto
* OVCS intervention

Hereâ€™s a **complete, precise, institution-grade answer** to your question:

> **How does your personal office handle equity/ownership in the Pamoja Federation Coop, other federation entities & ventures, the family estate, and other family member offices/businesses?**

Iâ€™ll break this down into clear, non-negotiable rules and mechanisms so that:

* Authority doesnâ€™t get captured by ownership.

# âœ¨ OVERALL PRINCIPLE:

**Your personal office (DESF) should never *own* controlling equity in federated entities or ventures â€” inside or outside the federation.**

Ownership must be structured so that:

* It does not create governance control.
* It does not confer capital claims outside permitted roles.
* It does not violate federation or commons constraints.

---

# A. **Your Personal Office: Allowed vs. Forbidden Holdings**

### **Allowed**

1. **Fixed-fee receivables** for services provided (governance, sequencing, design).

   * E.g., invoices for helping set up federation charters.
2. **Temporary custodial instruments** with sunset clauses.

   * E.g., transitional escrow holding until an entity is fully live.
3. **Non-voting units for transitional state tracking** where allowed by charter.

### **Forbidden**

âŒ No voting equity in:

* Pamoja Federation Coop
* Federation entities
* Cooperative ventures
  âŒ No financial claim on asset pools (no profit share, dividends, carried interest) beyond explicit fees.
  âŒ No ownership in family estate assets without firewall contracts.

**Why this matters:**
Equity implies *ownership + control + claim on asset value*. This mixes governance power with capital, which weâ€™ve explicitly forbidden in your ecosystem (authority â‰  capital).

---

# B. **Pamoja Federation Coop**

### Legal Logic

* Coop membership â‰  equity ownership.
* Federation coops use **membership units**, not stock.

### How DESF interacts

* DESF may be a **member** on behalf of a stewardship role (Class B/C), but:

  * It holds *membership rights*, not *capital rights*.
  * It cannot own coop resources.
  * It cannot receive distributions.

### Implementation Rules

1. **Membership units held in trust** â€” DESF holds them only as a *steward*.
2. **Sunset clause** â€” must auto-exit after governance transition.
3. **Non-transferable to personal accounts** â€” cannot flow into your balance sheet.

---

# C. **Federation Entities (Subsidiary Coops / Networks)**

These include:

* Moyo Collective
* Bahari Network
* Etc.

### Ownership Handling

* **DESF may help draft entities but does not own them.**
* Family office can provide seed contributions (money, social capital), but:

  * Must be **gifted or licensed**, not owned.
  * Must be **custodial with sunset**.

### Legal Vehicle Example

* **Time-boxed custodial membership units**
* **Non-financial participatory certificates**
* **Charter-enforced non-ownership status**

---

# D. **Ventures and Venture Coops**

Ventures â€” e.g., Nandi Mobility Company â€” *may be separate cooperative or corporate forms*.

### Two Design Patterns

#### **1) Coop Ventures (Worker/Member Coops)**

* DESF may hold **non-voting membership** during formation.
* Must exit membership upon:

  * Venture reach autonomous governance
  * Sunset period expires (e.g., 180 days after launch)

#### **2) Corporates / LLC Ventures**

* DESF may provide services but does **not take equity**.
* If *capital participation* is desired:

  * Use **Capital Note** (no ownership; fixed repayment rights only)
  * Or structured via **Mande Investment Group (MIG)** â€” not DESF

**Summary Rule:**

> DESF does not hold ownershipâ€”only *permissive, transitional, non-equity roles*.

---

# E. **Family Estate**

### The Eaton Family Estate Coop

This is a *distinct institutional container* that can:

* Hold family property
* Steward family member offices
* Define inter-office resource policies

**Key Distinctions**

* Family estate *may* hold assets structured as:

  * Trust interests
  * Patrimony units
  * Custodial holdings

**But MUST NEVER**

* Inherit federation governance authority
* Claim federation assets
* Use federation capital as its own wealth pool

### How DESF Interacts

* DESF may *advise* and *help form* the estate coop.
* DESF may act as an initial steward during formation, but:

  * Must exit stewardship per **sunset clause**.
  * Must never take estate assets into its own books.

---

# F. **Family Member Offices / Other Enterprises**

Each family member office or business can be:

* An independent entity (LLC, NPO, Coop)
* A licensee of templates and norms from DESF
* Governed by the estate coopâ€™s firewall policy

### How Ownership Works

#### **For Family Members**

1. **Independent incorporation**
2. **No federation governance roles by default**
3. **Estate coop has governance oversight (not ownership)**

   * Estate coop may hold membership units *only as a steward*, not proprietor
4. **Firewalled from federation equity**

### Template Rule

> Family member offices operate under *charter templates generated by DESF*, but they do not transfer capital or governance ownership back to DESF or estate without explicit policies.

---

# G. **Bridge Rules (Between Entities)**

## 1) **Temporary Custodianship**

DESF may temporarily hold:

* Membership units
* Non-economic rights
* Transitional certificates
  **Only if**
* Clearly documented
* Sunset date attached
* OVCS/Stewards approve

## 2) **Custodial Membership Does Not Equal Ownership**

Example:

> DESF can hold a membership certificate for a federation entity *on behalf of a steward* but has **no economic or voting rights** attached.

## 3) **Exit Triggers**

On ANY of:

* Time elapsed (e.g., 180 days)
* Federation governing milestone achieved
* Federation autonomy declared
* OVCS call

DESF **must transfer** custodial instruments to:

# 2ï¸âƒ£ GENERAL LIFECYCLES

## 2.1 MEMBER LIFECYCLE

**Rotation**

* Terms limited
* Independent review for renewal

## **Name:**

**Entity Genesis Framework (EGF)**

## **Description:**

The **Entity Genesis Framework (EGF)** is the **root artifact and canonical founding document** for any organizational entity created within your system of governance (e.g., personal office, estate coop, federation coop, venture entity). The EGF functions as the *origin point* in the artifact library, and it launches the entity into existence with full institutional clarity, authority grounding, and lifecycle support.

### **Purpose**

The EGF formalizes both **intention and structure** for an entity, ensuring it is:

* **Legally grounded**
* **Governance-complete**
* **Sequence-tied to Msingi & Ashe cycles**
* **Audit-ready for OVCS oversight**
* **Interoperable with federation and commons protocols**
* **Versioned and immutable in the artifact registry**

### **Core Roles**

The EGF acts as:

* **Charter container** â€” Holds the charter or articles defining the entityâ€™s purpose, powers, and limits.
* **Business blueprint** â€” Includes business plans, financial frameworks, and sustainability models.
* **Roadmap anchor** â€” Embeds sequence and milestone plans tied to Msingi phases.
* **Constitutional record** â€” Contains foundational governance rules and constraints.
* **Design library head** â€” Serves as the root index for all future documents: ideas, concepts, designs, reports, briefs, and evaluations.

### **Artifact Categories Typically Included**

1. **Charters / Constitutions**
2. **Business Plans & Models**
3. **Roadmaps / PI Plans / Sprint Maps**
4. **Governance Manuals & Constraint Policies**
5. **Stewardship & Authority Agreements**
6. **Immutable Verification Signatures**
7. **Msingi / Ashe Lifecycle Artifacts**
8. **Risk & Compliance Documentation**
9. **Insurance, Tax & Financial Frameworks**
10. **Contracts & Licenses**

### **Format & Structure**

The EGF is structured as a *container artifact* in your immutable ledger with fields such as:

* **Entity ID**
* **Entity Type**
* **Founding Timestamp**
* **Founders + Initial Stewards**
* **Charter Reference**
* **Artifact Pointers (hashes)**
* **Governance Ruleset Pointer**
* **Initial Roadmap**
* **Msingi Phase Assignments**
* **Constraints & Sunset Conditions**

### **Lifecycle Role**

Every entityâ€™s EGF is:

* **Created at inception**
* **Immutable once published**
* **Referenced by governance processes**
* **Updated only via formal amendment artifacts**
* **Audited on every Msingi phase transition**

It serves as the **genetic record** for the entityâ€™s institutional identity.

---

* **Entity** â€” Applies universally to any organizational form
* **Genesis** â€” Marks the *origin and identity*
* **Framework** â€” Not just a document; a living scaffold for evolution

## ðŸ§¬ **The First Document of the EGF**

### **Official Name**

**Founding Manifesto & Intent Declaration (FMID)**

Other acceptable synonyms you might see in organizational design include:

* **Founding Statement**
* **Inception Manifesto**
* **Genesis Declaration**
* **Entity Intent Charter**

But in your system â€” rooted in authority constraints, sequencing, and artifact truth â€” the canonical first document is the:

> ðŸ›ï¸ **Founding Manifesto & Intent Declaration (FMID)**

---

## ðŸŸ¡ **What the FMID Is**

The FMID is:

### âœ” The initial *intent artifact*

It expresses *why* the entity exists â€” **before anything else is defined**.

### âœ” A contract with reality

Not just a vision â€” it captures:

* Purpose
* Boundaries
* Non-goals
* Authority scope
* High-level metrics of success/failure

### âœ” The true â€œgenetic markerâ€

It is the first artifact stored in the EGF and the seed precedent for all subsequent charters, plans, policies, and governance docs.

---

## ðŸ§± How the FMID Fits in the Lifecycle

```
[FMID] â†’ [Charter / Constitution] â†’ [Roadmap] â†’ [Business Plan] â†’ [Governance Rules] â†’ [Operational Artifacts]
```

So the FMID is the **actual first artifact** of the EGF. Everything else flows from it and references it.

---

## ðŸ“œ **What the FMID Contains**

Below are the *required fields and sections* of an FMID:

### **1) Entity Name**

* Formal name (even if provisional)
* Legal form pending incorporation

### **2) Founding Timestamp**

* Exact date/time of declaration
* Jurisdiction reference if relevant

### **3) Purpose Statement (Why Now?)**

* Clearly articulated mission (1â€“2 paragraphs)
* Short, medium, long-term intent
* Non-overlapping against existing entities

### **4) Non-Goals**

* What the entity *will not do*
* What it explicitly rejects
* Alignment to governance limits

### **5) Operational Sphere**

* Domain of action, problem space
* Boundaries of authority
* Initial scope without details

### **6) Authority Dependencies**

* Which constraint authorities it defers to (e.g., OVCS, Estate firewall)
* Which potential stewards are relevant

### **7) Initial Stakeholders**

* Navigator / Founder
* Initial Stewards
* Known collaborators

### **8) Minimum Viability Criteria**

* What must be true for this intent to be considered â€œbornâ€
* Usually a checklist that scaffolds the next artifact (the charter)

### **9) Risks & Failure Conditions**

* What counts as termination or non-viability
* Red lines the entity must not cross

### **10) Artifact Lineage Pointer**

* A unique artifact identifier (hash, UUID)
* Placeholder for future linkage

---

## ðŸ“¥ The FMID in a Sample Template Form

Hereâ€™s a **brief template** you can use to create one for *any* entity:

```
FOUNDING MANIFESTO & INTENT DECLARATION (FMID)

1) ENTITY NAME:
   - [e.g., â€œDominic Eaton Software Engineering Firmâ€]

2) FOUNDING DATE:
   - [YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS UTC]

3) PURPOSE:
   - [High-level mission]

4) NON-GOALS:
   - [Explicit exclusions]

5) OPERATIONAL SPHERE:
   - [Scope boundaries]

6) AUTHORITY DEPENDENCIES:
   - [List OVCS, Estate, Commons, Laws]

7) INITIAL STAKEHOLDERS:
   - Founder: [Name]
   - Initial Stewards: [Names + roles]
   - Partners: [Optional]

8) MINIMUM VIABILITY CRITERIA:
   - [Conditions that must be true for the entity to proceed]

9) RISKS & FAILURE CONDITIONS:
   - [Short list of intolerable outcomes]

10) ARTIFACT LINEAGE:
   - FMID-ID: [UUID or Hash]
   - Next expected artifact (Charter reference placeholder)
```

---

## ðŸ§  Why FMID Comes *Before* the Charter

* The **FMID declares intent** but does *not* yet give legal powers.
* The **Charter** formalizes authority *after* the intent is established.

This is similar to:

* **Kano â†’ Ndebe â†’ Charter** in the Msingi cycle
* Intent â†’ Concept â†’ Formal authority

In other words:

> **Intent precedes Authority.**

---

## ðŸ›¡ FMID as an Artifact

As with all artifacts in your ecosystem:

* It gets a **ledger entry**
* It has a cryptographic **hash**
* It has an artifact ID
* It is referenced by later artifacts
* It can be audited by OVCS

FMID is the **root of the artifact chain**.

### **2. DECLARATION OF INTENT**

**2.1 Purpose**
The purpose of the *Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm* (hereafter â€œDESFâ€ or â€œthe Officeâ€) is to serve as an independent **institutional design, sequencing, governance engineering, and constraint authority enablement organization**. DESF constructs, sequences, and authorizes entities (cooperatives, platforms, commons, federated institutions) using structured methods, including the Msingi and Ashe cycles. DESF provides governance architecture, sequencing artifacts, and constraint frameworks without capturing operational or capital ownership of the entities it helps establish.

**2.2 Long-Term Vision**
DESF exists to catalyze resilient, self-governing institutions, minimizing founder dependency while maximizing systemic coherence. DESFâ€™s engagements are time-bounded, traceable, and audited by external governance constraints (e.g., OVCS) to guarantee alignment with institutional independence and ethical stewardship.

### **3. NON-GOALS (BOUNDARIES)**

The following are explicitly *not* objectives of DESF:

* DESF **shall not hold equity or controlling ownership** of any entity that it sequences or empowers.
* DESF **shall not act as a capital investment vehicle** or capital-allocating entity.
* DESF **shall not accumulate profit** beyond mission-aligned operating fees.
* DESF **shall not exercise governance authority** over entities beyond issuing sequencing artifacts and governance design artifacts.
* DESF **shall not have voting control in federated governance bodies** by virtue of founding.

These non-goals are fundamental and enforced by charter constraints and OVCS auditing.

## **Preamble**

We, the undersigned, in recognition of the need for rigorous institutional grounding, hereby adopt this **Constitution** as the supreme organizing document of the *Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm* (â€œDESFâ€ or â€œOfficeâ€). This Constitution defines the fundamental principles, authority limits, governance foundations, and institutional behavior for the Office as it operates under the Entity Genesis Framework (EGF).

---

## **Article I â€” Identity & Purpose**

### Section 1.1 Name

The legal name of this entity is

> **Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm**
> (hereafter â€œDESFâ€).

### Section 1.2 Mission

DESF exists to design and implement governance architecture, sequencing cycles, and constraint systems for cooperative ecosystems, ensuring systemic viability without capturing authority or capital.

### Section 1.3 Vision

To enable institutions that are resilient, constraint-aware, and capable of self-governance without undue human dependency.

---

## **Article II â€” Foundational Constraints**

### Section 2.1 Non-Ownership Principle

DESF shall *not* hold governing equity in any entity it sequences or supports.

### Section 2.2 Capital & Asset Separation

Capital participation for DESF shall be limited to operational funds; any investment in ventures shall be undertaken through appropriate conduits such as Mande Investment Group (MIG), and not held on DESF books.

### Section 2.3 Authority Hierarchy

DESF acknowledges the supremacy of:

* **OVCS** (Obatala Venture Constraint System) for constraint authority
* **Commons frameworks** for stewardship and asset logic
* **Federation governance bodies** where interaction is permitted

---

## **Article III â€” Institutional Lifecycle**

### Section 3.1 Entity Lifecycle

DESFâ€™s institutional lifecycle includes:

1. Intention (FMID)
2. Constitutional establishment
3. Charter adoption
4. Operational sequencing
5. Knowledge fixation and archive
6. Sunset or transformation

### Section 3.2 Sunset & Dissolution

DESF may be dissolved by:

* 2/3 Governance Council vote
* OVCS determination of mission completion
  Assets and knowledge artifacts shall be transferred to an appropriate commons or archival trust.

---

## **Article IV â€” Governance Structure**

### Section 4.1 Governance Council

The primary governing body of DESF is the **Governance Council**, composed of:

* Founder / Navigator (Class E)
* Constraint Steward (Class C)
* Systems Steward (Class B)
* Human Viability Steward (Class D)
* Independent Advisor (optional)

### Section 4.2 Authority Limits

No single individual may:

* Override Charter constraints
* Unilaterally bind the institution
* Alter constitutional constraints without Council and OVCS ratification

---

## **Article V â€” Stewardship & Rotation**

### Section 5.1 Steward Classes

DESF recognizes the following steward classes with defined roles:

* Class A: Operational Staff Stewards
* Class B: Strategic Stewards
* Class C: Independent Constraint Stewards
* Class D: Human Viability Stewards
* Class E: Founder / Navigator (non-permanent, constrained authority)

### Section 5.2 Rotation Rules

Stewards serve fixed terms and may not exceed two consecutive terms without Governance Council and OVCS approval.

---

## **Article VI â€” Artifact Ledger & Transparency**

## âœ… What â€œLegal Document Packageâ€ Means

A *Legal Document Package* is a structured bundle of:

1. **Title Page**
2. **Body Text** â€” with legally enforceable language
3. **Execution / Signature Pages**
4. **Notary Blocks (if required)**

Each document is designed to be **self-standing**, meaning it can be:

* Filed with an authority
* Executed by signatories
* Uploaded into your artifact ledger
* Used as proof of governance in audits

# A) **CONVERSION PATH â€” LLC â†’ CORPORATION**

**Purpose:** A legally compliant mechanism to convert your *Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm, LLC* into a *corporation* (e.g., a C-Corporation or Public Benefit Corporation) at the appropriate time.

This includes:

1. Conversion Power Clause (to insert into your LLC Operating Agreement)
2. Statutory Conversion Resolution
3. Model Plan of Conversion
4. Articles of Incorporation (template for the new corporation)

---

## 1) **Operating Agreement â€” Conversion Power Clause**

**Insert as Section *X* of your DESF LLC Operating Agreement**

```
Section X â€” Conversion to Corporation

X.1 Authority to Convert.
The Company shall have the power to convert into a corporation (the â€œConverted Entityâ€) pursuant to applicable state law, including but not limited to Section ____ of the Missouri Revised Statutes (or the corresponding provisions of the law of the State of Organization), and this Section.

X.2 Conditions Precedent to Conversion.
No conversion may occur unless:
(a) A written Plan of Conversion is adopted by a Supermajority Vote (defined as at least 67%) of the Members;
(b) All outstanding membership interests, capital accounts, and constituent documents (including but not limited to this Operating Agreement and associated exhibits) are reconciled and either assumed by or extinguished in favor of the Converted Entity;
(c) A certificate of conversion and Articles of Incorporation for the Converted Entity are properly filed with the applicable Secretary of State; and
(d) Any required notifications, consents, or filings required by federal or state law (including IRS compliance if tax-status impact occurs) are completed.

X.3 Conversion Mechanics.
Upon approval, the Manager shall prepare or cause to be prepared the Plan of Conversion, negotiate required terms, file all required instruments with the appropriate authorities, and oversee the transition of assets, liabilities, contracts, books, and records to the Converted Entity.

X.4 Successor Liability.
The Converted Entity shall be the legal successor of the Company for all purposes, and the Company shall cease to exist upon the effective date of the conversion.

X.5 Notice.
Notice of the intent to consider conversion shall be provided to all Members no less than thirty (30) days prior to the vote.

X.6 OVCS & Artifact Ledger Integration.
Any conversion plan and materials shall be archived in the Entity Genesis Framework (EGF) immutable artifact ledger with cross-references to FMID and relevant roadmap artifacts, and be subject to visible review by the OVCS liaison.
```

## 3) **Plan of Conversion (Template)**

```
PLAN OF CONVERSION
DOMINIC EATON SOFTWARE ENGINEERING FIRM, LLC
TO
[Name of Corporation], INC.

This Plan of Conversion (the â€œPlanâ€) is entered into by Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm, LLC (the â€œCompanyâ€), pursuant to Section ___ of the Missouri LLC Law.

1. Conversion Entities.
   a. Converting Entity: Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm, LLC
   b. Converted Entity: [Name of Corporation], a corporation organized under the laws of [State], with principal office at [Address].

2. Terms and Conditions of Conversion.
   a. Legal Effect.
      Upon conversion, the Company shall cease to be an LLC and shall be a corporation.
   b. Capital Interests.
      Membership interests shall convert to shares of the Converted Entity as follows:
      - [Member Name] â†’ [Number & Class of Shares]
```
